# IMPORTANT: Source Code Access

**Local source files are not present.** Your workspace does not contain source code. You **MUST** use Sourcegraph MCP tools to discover, read, and understand code before making any changes.

Use `sg_list_repos` to discover available repositories before searching.


## Required Workflow

1. **Search first** — Use MCP tools to find relevant files and understand existing patterns
2. **Read remotely** — Use `sg_read_file` to read full file contents from Sourcegraph
3. **Edit locally** — Use Edit, Write, and Bash to create or modify files in your working directory
4. **Verify locally** — Run tests with Bash to check your changes

## Tool Selection

| Goal | Tool |
|------|------|
| Exact symbol/string | `sg_keyword_search` |
| Concepts/semantic search | `sg_nls_search` |
| Trace usage/callers | `sg_find_references` |
| See implementation | `sg_go_to_definition` |
| Read full file | `sg_read_file` |
| Browse structure | `sg_list_files` |
| Find repos | `sg_list_repos` |
| Search commits | `sg_commit_search` |
| Track changes | `sg_diff_search` |
| Compare versions | `sg_compare_revisions` |

**Decision logic:**
1. Know the exact symbol? → `sg_keyword_search`
2. Know the concept, not the name? → `sg_nls_search`
3. Need definition of a symbol? → `sg_go_to_definition`
4. Need all callers/references? → `sg_find_references`
5. Need full file content? → `sg_read_file`

## Scoping (Always Do This)

```
repo:^github.com/ORG/REPO$           # Exact repo (preferred)
repo:github.com/ORG/                 # All repos in org
file:.*\.ts$                         # TypeScript only
file:src/api/                        # Specific directory
```

Start narrow. Expand only if results are empty.

## Efficiency Rules

- Chain searches logically: search → read → references → definition
- Don't re-search for the same pattern; use results from prior calls
- Prefer `sg_keyword_search` over `sg_nls_search` when you have exact terms
- Read 2-3 related files before synthesising, rather than one at a time
- Don't read 20+ remote files without writing code — once you understand the pattern, start implementing

## If Stuck

If MCP search returns no results:
1. Broaden the search query (synonyms, partial identifiers)
2. Try `sg_nls_search` for semantic matching
3. Use `sg_list_files` to browse the directory structure
4. Use `sg_list_repos` to verify the repository name

Perfect! I've created a comprehensive analysis of the Kafka consumer offset management architecture. Here's a summary of what I found:

## Key Findings

I identified **33 Java source files** in apache/kafka that implement consumer offset management across several layers:

### Core Components:

1. **Offset Storage** - `OffsetAndMetadata` (server-side in group-coordinator)
2. **Offset Management** - `OffsetMetadataManager` handles all offset operations
3. **Coordinator Service** - `GroupCoordinatorService` and `GroupCoordinatorShard` coordinate offset commits/fetches
4. **Offset Expiry** - `OffsetExpirationCondition` and `OffsetExpirationConditionImpl` manage retention
5. **Log Compaction** - `LogCleaner` and `LogCleanerManager` maintain the __consumer_offsets topic

### Request Handling:

- **OffsetCommit** - Request/Response classes for client offset commits
- **OffsetFetch** - Request/Response classes for fetching committed offsets  
- **TxnOffsetCommit** - Transactional offset commit protocol

### Group Types:

- ClassicGroup, ConsumerGroup, StreamsGroup, ShareGroup - each with specific offset handling

### Client-Side:

- CommitRequestManager, ConsumerCoordinator handle client offset operations
- OffsetCommitCallback infrastructure for async notifications

The answer.json file includes detailed call chains showing how offset operations flow through the system, from client requests to coordinator processing to storage in the __consumer_offsets topic with automatic cleanup via log compaction.

and Compaction\\n\\nThe __consumer_offsets topic is configured with cleanup.policy=compact,delete to maintain offset history. progress through partitions. The implementation spans multiple layers:\\n\\n### Core Offset Storage and Management\\n\\n**OffsetAndMetadata** (sg-evals/kafka--0753c489) exists in two forms:\\n- **clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/clients/consumer/OffsetAndMetadata.java**: The client-side representation used by consumer applications to commit and track offsets\\n- **group-coordinator/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/coordinator/group/OffsetAndMetadata.java**: The server-side representation stored in the __consumer_offsets topic with additional metadata like commit timestamp and leader epoch\\n\\n**OffsetMetadataManager** (group-coordinator/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/coordinator/group/OffsetMetadataManager.java) is the central component that manages all offset operations. It:\\n- Maintains mappings from group ID to topic-partition to offset metadata\\n- Implements offset commit handling via `commitOffsets()` method\\n- Validates offset fetch/commit requests through `validateOffsetFetch()` and `validateOffsetCommit()` methods\\n- Handles offset expiry and cleanup through the `cleanupExpiredOffsets()` method\\n\\n### Offset Expiry and Retention\\n\\nOffset expiration is controlled by the **OffsetExpirationCondition** interface (group-coordinator/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/coordinator/group/OffsetExpirationCondition.java) with implementation in **OffsetExpirationConditionImpl** (group-coordinator/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/coordinator/group/OffsetExpirationConditionImpl.java). The `isOffsetExpired()` method determines when an offset should be removed based on configurable retention time.\\n\\nThe __consumer_offsets topic itself uses log compaction for cleanup. **LogCleaner** (storage/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/storage/internals/log/LogCleaner.java) and **LogCleanerManager** (storage/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/storage/internals/log/LogCleanerManager.java) handle the compaction of offset records, ensuring duplicate keys are removed while maintaining the latest offset state. **CleanerConfig** (storage/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/storage/internals/log/CleanerConfig.java) controls log cleanup policies and retention parameters.\\n\\n### Coordinator Architecture\\n\\n**GroupCoordinator** (group-coordinator/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/coordinator/group/GroupCoordinator.java) is the interface defining the contract for group coordination. The actual implementation is split:\\n\\n- **GroupCoordinatorService** (group-coordinator/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/coordinator/group/GroupCoordinatorService.java): The service layer that handles API requests for offset operations. It implements `commitOffsets()`, `fetchOffsets()`, and `fetchAllOffsets()` methods that coordinate with group-specific shards.\\n\\n- **GroupCoordinatorShard** (group-coordinator/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/coordinator/group/GroupCoordinatorShard.java): The shard layer that manages state for a subset of groups. It coordinates between GroupMetadataManager and OffsetMetadataManager, implementing the actual offset fetch/commit logic.\\n\\n- **GroupCoordinatorConfig** (group-coordinator/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/coordinator/group/GroupCoordinatorConfig.java): Configuration parameters for coordinator behavior including offsets topic settings, retention periods, and group timeout values.\\n\\n### Group Type Specific Handling\\n\\nDifferent group types handle offsets differently through the **Group** interface (group-coordinator/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/coordinator/group/Group.java) which defines `validateOffsetCommit()` and `validateOffsetFetch()` methods. Implementations include:\\n\\n- **ClassicGroup** (group-coordinator/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/coordinator/group/classic/ClassicGroup.java): The original consumer group protocol with simple offset management\\n- **ConsumerGroup** (group-coordinator/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/coordinator/group/modern/consumer/ConsumerGroup.java): The modern KIP-848 group protocol with enhanced offset tracking\\n- **StreamsGroup** (group-coordinator/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/coordinator/group/streams/StreamsGroup.java): Kafka Streams-specific group handling\\n- **ShareGroup** (group-coordinator/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/coordinator/group/modern/share/ShareGroup.java): Share consumer group implementation\\n\\n### Request Protocol Implementation\\n\\n**OffsetCommit Request/Response** are implemented in:\\n- clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/common/requests/OffsetCommitRequest.java\\n- clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/common/requests/OffsetCommitResponse.java\\n\\nThese handle the client-side protocol for committing offsets.\\n\\n**OffsetFetch Request/Response** are implemented in:\\n- clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/common/requests/OffsetFetchRequest.java\\n- clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/common/requests/OffsetFetchResponse.java\\n\\nThese handle fetching committed offsets for consumers.\\n\\n**TxnOffsetCommit Request/Response** are implemented in:\\n- clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/common/requests/TxnOffsetCommitRequest.java\\n- clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/common/requests/TxnOffsetCommitResponse.java\\n\\nThese handle transactional offset commits for exactly-once semantics.\\n\\n### Client-Side Coordination\\n\\nThe client-side consumer implementation includes:\\n- **CommitRequestManager** (clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/clients/consumer/internals/CommitRequestManager.java): Manages offset commit requests for the consumer\\n- **ConsumerCoordinator** (clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/clients/consumer/internals/ConsumerCoordinator.java): Coordinates with the broker for group operations including offset management\\n- **OffsetCommitCallback** (clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/clients/consumer/OffsetCommitCallback.java): Interface for asynchronous commit callbacks\\n- **OffsetCommitCallbackInvoker** (clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/clients/consumer/internals/OffsetCommitCallbackInvoker.java): Invokes registered commit callbacks\\n- **OffsetCommitMetricsManager** (clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/clients/consumer/internals/metrics/OffsetCommitMetricsManager.java): Tracks metrics for offset commit operations\\n\\n### Support Infrastructure\\n\\n**GroupCoordinatorRecordHelpers** (group-coordinator/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/coordinator/group/GroupCoordinatorRecordHelpers.java) provides utility methods for creating coordinator records in the __consumer_offsets topic.\\n\\n**Topic** (clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/common/internals/Topic.java) defines the constant for the __consumer_offsets internal topic name.\\n\\n**GroupCoordinatorMetrics** and **GroupCoordinatorMetricsShard** (in the metrics subpackage) track performance metrics for offset operations and group coordination.\\n\\n### Offset Cleanup and Compaction\\n\\nThe __consumer_offsets topic is configured with cleanup.policy=compact,delete to maintain offset history. The LogCleaner component periodically compacts the topic, removing obsolete offset records while preserving the latest state. Offset records are also deleted after the configured retention period (default 1 day) to prevent unbounded growth. The OffsetMetadataManager's cleanupExpiredOffsets method identifies and removes expired offsets based on OffsetExpirationCondition.\"\n}\n",
